- [profile basis: source_fact; source: src_d04a80ddf2c85472] project_summary: reducing long-context inference latency and power on mobile NPUs

## 3 Problem and Opportunity Areas

- [candidate hypothesis] On-device long-context LLM decoding runs every transformer layer at a single static quantization bit-width, yet layers differ greatly in quantization sensitivity: one fixed precision either over-spends NPU energy on error-tolerant layers or injects accuracy loss and latency stalls on sensitive ones. During sustained long-context decoding the mobile NPU also thermally throttles, destabilizing per-token latency, and no per-layer precision policy reacts to that thermal state.
- [candidate hypothesis] On-device long-context decoding grows the KV-cache monotonically as tokens are generated. Allocating it in many small pages fragments the NPU's memory and inflates address-translation and DMA-descriptor overhead, so per-token latency climbs with context length and the memory system thrashes; there is also not enough on-device memory to keep a very long context fully resident at full precision.
- [candidate hypothesis] On-device NPU decoding is memory-bandwidth-bound: the quantized KV-cache plus per-block weight quantization metadata (scales, zero-points, low-bit residuals) must be re-read every step, and storing them in fixed-width codes wastes the very bandwidth that dominates decode latency. Yet per-block quantization parameters are strongly correlated across neighboring blocks, attention heads, and decode positions - a redundancy left unexploited by fixed-width storage.

## 6 Final Candidates

### 1. Sensitivity-adaptive per-layer precision scheduling for on-device LLM decoding with decode-step continuity smoothing and NPU thermal feedback
- Problem: On-device long-context LLM decoding runs every transformer layer at a single static quantization bit-width, yet layers differ greatly in quantization sensitivity: one fixed precision either over-spends NPU energy on error-tolerant layers or injects accuracy loss and latency stalls on sensitive ones. During sustained long-context decoding the mobile NPU also thermally throttles, destabilizing per-token latency, and no per-layer precision policy reacts to that thermal state. [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- Proposed mechanism: A lightweight per-layer quantization-sensitivity estimator (a load-time calibration proxy from each layer's activation dynamic range plus a running online estimate) drives an adaptive precision controller that assigns each layer a bit-width for the current decode step, in the same way the referenced streaming server sets a per-frame quantization parameter from estimated frame data-variation. A decode-step continuity term smooths bit-width transitions across successive generated tokens - the analog of the reference's image-continuity QP refinement - so precision does not oscillate token-to-token and thrash the NPU kernel dispatcher. A thermal-feedback loop samples NPU die temperature and power state and biases the controller toward lower precision as thermal headroom shrinks, a control input the cloud-server reference has no need for and does not consider. [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- Key components and interactions [candidate hypothesis]: per-layer quantization-sensitivity estimator, adaptive per-layer precision controller (bit-width / QP-analog map), decode-step continuity smoother, NPU thermal and power-state sensor loop, mixed-precision kernel dispatcher; the sensitivity estimator feeds a per-layer sensitivity signal to the precision controller each decode step, the continuity smoother constrains how far the controller may move a layer's bit-width between consecutive tokens, the thermal loop biases the controller's bit-width targets downward as NPU thermal headroom shrinks, the kernel dispatcher selects the matching mixed-precision kernel for each layer's assigned bit-width
- Expected technical effects [creative suggestion]: reduced NPU energy per generated token at a bounded accuracy loss versus static precision, smaller per-token latency variance under sustained thermal load, fewer precision-oscillation-induced kernel re-dispatches
- User/domain fit [profile-based inference]: edge AI inference systems
- Relationship to the closest prior art: 인공지능 신경망의 층별 속성에 기초한 적응형 티어 분류 및 양자화 시스템 및 방법 (1020260054547) [@ev_e532da120d690723]
- Differentiating features: A per-layer quantization-sensitivity estimator drives an adaptive precision controller that sets each layer's bit-width per decode step, smoothed across decode steps for continuity and biased downward by an NPU thermal-feedback loop., A per-layer bit-width schedule for each decode step and the resulting quantized generated tokens., Full-precision per-layer weights and activations are mapped to a per-layer, per-decode-step variable bit-width representation derived from smoothed sensitivity and thermal signals. [@ev_e532da120d690723]
- Implementation and validation example [creative suggestion]: A Llama-class decoder on a mobile NPU with 8/4/2-bit mixed-precision kernels; the sensitivity proxy is computed once at model load from a short calibration prompt and refined online from per-layer activation ranges, and the thermal loop polls the NPU thermal sensor every few decode steps and shifts each layer's bit-width target when the die nears its throttle threshold.; At a fixed average bit-width, compare task accuracy and perplexity against a static-precision baseline; under a fixed thermal envelope compare tokens/sec and joules per generated token; and measure p99 per-token latency variance across a long-context decode to confirm the continuity smoother reduces precision-oscillation stalls.
- Uncertainties and follow-up questions [hypothesis]: What calibration-prompt length yields a stable per-layer sensitivity proxy without inflating model load time?, How aggressively can precision drop under thermal pressure before task accuracy degrades unacceptably for the target workload?
- Evaluation axes:
  - differentiation: confidence medium / rationale Beyond static or uniformly mixed-precision quantization, this candidate ties per-layer bit-width to an online quantization-sensitivity signal and adds an NPU thermal and power-state feedback input; the closest research-phase reference (ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb) adapts a quantization parameter to content variation for cloud video frames and has no notion of transformer-layer sensitivity or on-device thermal budget. / coverage Research-phase evidence covers adaptive quantization-parameter setting for video (ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb); it does not yet cover on-device mixed-precision scheduling or thermal-aware inference prior art, which the finalist-specific audit re-search must retrieve. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
  - technical_feasibility: confidence high / rationale Every building block already ships on device - mixed-precision (8/4/2-bit) NPU kernels, activation-range calibration, and thermal/power-state sensors - so the effort is integration and control-loop tuning rather than new hardware; the main feasibility risk is the online sensitivity proxy's stability. / coverage Feasibility is judged from the mechanism's reliance on already-available NPU capabilities; the research corpus does not directly benchmark such a control loop, a gap the audit does not close since it is prior-art retrieval, not measurement. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
  - utility_significance: confidence high / rationale Directly targets the profile's stated problem - KV-cache memory and thermal budgets causing latency spikes for long contexts - by trading precision for energy and latency stability under thermal load, a first-order concern for sustained on-device decoding. / coverage Utility is grounded in the profile's observed problem and expertise; the evidence corpus confirms the domain's activity but does not quantify the specific energy/latency trade, which remains an empirical open question. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
### 2. Large-page-backed, growth-aware KV-cache allocator with precision-tiered cold-entry migration for on-device NPU inference
- Problem: On-device long-context decoding grows the KV-cache monotonically as tokens are generated. Allocating it in many small pages fragments the NPU's memory and inflates address-translation and DMA-descriptor overhead, so per-token latency climbs with context length and the memory system thrashes; there is also not enough on-device memory to keep a very long context fully resident at full precision. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- Proposed mechanism: The KV-cache is served from a small pool of pre-reserved large pages sized to context-length milestones, applying the referenced idea of managing LLM memory in huge-page units - but adapted from a one-time, install-time allocation of static weights on a server GPU to the dynamic, decode-time growth of the KV-cache on a memory-constrained NPU. A growth manager appends newly generated keys/values into the current large page and only faults a new large page at a milestone boundary, so the number of DMA descriptors and translation entries scales with the number of large pages, not with token count. A tiering manager tracks per-head attention recency and migrates cold KV entries into a separate lower-precision large-page pool, freeing hot-pool capacity and restoring entries on demand. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- Key components and interactions [candidate hypothesis]: pre-reserved large-page pool, decode-time growth manager, per-head attention-recency tracker, precision-tiered cold-entry migration manager, hot and cold large-page KV pools; the growth manager appends new keys/values into the active large page and faults a new large page only at milestone boundaries, the recency tracker marks KV entries cold when their heads stop attending to them, the migration manager moves cold entries from the full-precision hot pool to the quantized cold pool and restores them on demand, address translation and DMA descriptors scale with the number of large pages rather than the number of tokens
- Expected technical effects [creative suggestion]: per-token latency that stays flatter as context length grows, reduced address-translation and DMA-descriptor overhead, longer resident context within a fixed on-device memory budget
- User/domain fit [profile-based inference]: edge AI inference systems
- Relationship to the closest prior art: 메모리관리장치 및 추론 성능 가속화 방법 (1020240066856) [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- Differentiating features: A large-page-backed allocator appends KV growth into the active large page and faults a new large page only at milestones, while a tiering manager migrates cold KV entries into a separate quantized large-page pool., A large-page-resident KV-cache layout plus a demoted quantized cold-KV pool with an on-demand restore path., A per-token growing KV stream is packed into a bounded set of large pages, and cold full-precision KV entries are transformed into lower-precision cold-pool entries. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- Implementation and validation example [creative suggestion]: A decoder on a mobile NPU reserves, for example, 2 MB large pages; the hot pool holds recent full-precision KV in a handful of large pages while the cold pool holds quantized KV, and the growth manager appends to the active large page each step while the tiering manager demotes least-recently-attended entries once the hot pool crosses an occupancy threshold.; Plot per-token latency against context length and compare the slope to a small-page baseline; count TLB misses and DMA descriptors at a fixed context; measure the resident context length achievable within a fixed memory budget; and quantify any task-accuracy impact from cold-tier quantization.
- Uncertainties and follow-up questions [hypothesis]: What large-page size best trades internal fragmentation against descriptor and translation savings on the target NPU?, How does cold-tier quantization precision interact with tasks that re-attend to old context, such as retrieval-style prompts?
- Evaluation axes:
  - differentiation: confidence medium / rationale The huge-page memory-management reference (ev_019c344b7b377649) optimizes a one-time, install-time allocation of static LLM weights on a server GPU; this candidate's delta is applying large-page backing to the dynamically growing KV-cache with on-demand eviction and a precision-tiered cold pool - a moving, decode-time target the reference does not treat. / coverage Research-phase evidence covers huge-page allocation for static LLM weights; it does not cover dynamic KV-cache allocators or precision-tiered eviction on NPUs, a gap for the audit re-search to probe. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
  - technical_feasibility: confidence medium / rationale Large-page allocation and DMA-descriptor control are platform-specific on mobile NPUs, so portability is a real risk; the growth/eviction logic and per-head attention-recency tracking are otherwise straightforward, giving moderate overall feasibility. / coverage Feasibility depends on NPU memory-system features (large pages, descriptor control) that the research corpus does not enumerate per platform; this hardware-portability question is outside what prior-art retrieval can settle. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
  - utility_significance: confidence high / rationale KV-cache memory is the profile's central pain point; keeping per-token latency flat as context grows and extending resident context within a fixed memory budget is highly valuable for long-context on-device use. / coverage Utility maps directly onto the profile's observed problem; the corpus establishes that KV-cache memory is an active concern but does not measure the allocator's latency-slope benefit. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
### 3. Context-adaptive entropy coding of on-device KV-cache and weight quantization parameters using transformer-structure contexts
- Problem: On-device NPU decoding is memory-bandwidth-bound: the quantized KV-cache plus per-block weight quantization metadata (scales, zero-points, low-bit residuals) must be re-read every step, and storing them in fixed-width codes wastes the very bandwidth that dominates decode latency. Yet per-block quantization parameters are strongly correlated across neighboring blocks, attention heads, and decode positions - a redundancy left unexploited by fixed-width storage. [@ev_01e10740134145d2]
- Proposed mechanism: The per-block quantization scales/zero-points and low-bit KV residuals are encoded with a binary arithmetic coder whose contexts are chosen in the referenced style - a distinct context for the first bin and separate contexts for the remaining magnitude bins - but the object being coded is the on-device quantizer's own quantization parameters, and the context index is derived from transformer structure (a neighboring block's scale, the attention head, and the decode position) rather than from spatial video neighbors. A hardware-light decoder-side context model reconstructs the values during the NPU read, so the coding is lossless with respect to the already-quantized tensor. [@ev_01e10740134145d2]
- Key components and interactions [candidate hypothesis]: per-block quantization-parameter and residual extractor, context selector keyed on transformer structure (neighbor block scale, head, decode position), context-adaptive binary arithmetic encoder (first-bin / other-bin contexts), hardware-light decoder-side context model, NPU inline-decode path before the attention matmul; the extractor emits per-block scales/zero-points and low-bit residuals as binary symbols, the context selector maps each symbol to a context from the neighboring block scale, head, and decode position, the arithmetic encoder codes the first bin and the remaining magnitude bins under their separate contexts, the decoder-side model reconstructs the quantization parameters inline during the NPU read before the attention matmul
- Expected technical effects [creative suggestion]: fewer bytes read per token for the KV-cache and quantization metadata, higher decode throughput on bandwidth-bound NPUs, no change to task accuracy, since coding is lossless with respect to the quantized values
- User/domain fit [profile-based inference]: edge AI inference systems
- Relationship to the closest prior art: 가변 양자화 파라미터 기반의 영상 부호화 및 복호화 방법 및 장치 (1020220136417) [@ev_e1f134720cc61bc3]
- Differentiating features: A context-adaptive binary arithmetic coder encodes per-block quantization scales/zero-points and low-bit KV residuals using first-bin and other-bin contexts indexed by transformer structure, decoded inline on the NPU., A compact arithmetic-coded representation of the quantization parameters and residuals, and the losslessly reconstructed quantized tensor on read., Fixed-width per-block quantization parameters and residuals are transformed into a context-adaptive arithmetic-coded bitstream and losslessly reconstructed on read. [@ev_e1f134720cc61bc3]
- Implementation and validation example [creative suggestion]: For a 4-bit per-block-quantized KV-cache, each block's scale delta and its low-bit residuals are coded with a small context-adaptive binary arithmetic coder; the context for a block is selected from the previous block's scale bucket, the head index, and the decode step, and the NPU decodes it inline before the attention matmul.; Compare bytes per token for the KV-cache and quantization metadata against a fixed-width baseline; measure decode tokens/sec on a bandwidth-bound NPU; count the coder's per-block overhead cycles; and confirm bit-exact reconstruction of the quantized tensor (lossless with respect to the quantized values).
- Uncertainties and follow-up questions [hypothesis]: Does the inline arithmetic-decode cost stay below the bandwidth it saves on the target NPU?, Which transformer-structure signal (neighbor scale, head, or position) contributes most of the context gain, so the model can stay hardware-light?
- Evaluation axes:
  - differentiation: confidence medium / rationale Coding the quantizer's own per-block parameters with transformer-structure contexts is a distinct angle from the video-QP-transmission reference (ev_01e10740134145d2); the coding tool is borrowed but the coded object and the context source differ substantially, and this angle is less represented in the research-phase corpus. / coverage Research-phase evidence covers context-adaptive arithmetic coding of video QP (ev_01e10740134145d2); it does not cover entropy coding of on-device KV/weight quantization metadata, a gap for the audit re-search. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_01e10740134145d2]
  - technical_feasibility: confidence low / rationale The central risk is that inline, largely serial arithmetic decoding on a parallel NPU may cost more than the memory bandwidth it saves; this makes feasibility the weakest of the three finalists and dependent on the decode-cost-versus-bandwidth trade holding on the target hardware. / coverage Feasibility rests on an on-device decode-cost trade that the research corpus does not measure; prior-art retrieval cannot resolve whether inline decode pays for itself on a given NPU. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_01e10740134145d2]
  - utility_significance: confidence medium / rationale Reducing KV and metadata bytes read per token helps a bandwidth-bound NPU, but the benefit is contingent on decode overhead staying small, making the utility narrower and more conditional than the other two finalists. / coverage Utility is conditional on the feasibility trade; the corpus confirms bandwidth pressure is real for on-device decoding but does not quantify this coder's net saving. / limitations Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run. / gaps none [@ev_01e10740134145d2]

## 7 Candidate Comparison Matrix

- Ordering below follows the shortlist priority recorded for each candidate. It is not an ordering by axis score.
- Axis figures are not shown: they are author-supplied inputs, are never computed by this tool, and never determine candidate order.
### 1. Sensitivity-adaptive per-layer precision scheduling for on-device LLM decoding with decode-step continuity smoothing and NPU thermal feedback [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- differentiation: Beyond static or uniformly mixed-precision quantization, this candidate ties per-layer bit-width to an online quantization-sensitivity signal and adds an NPU thermal and power-state feedback input; the closest research-phase reference (ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb) adapts a quantization parameter to content variation for cloud video frames and has no notion of transformer-layer sensitivity or on-device thermal budget. Coverage: Research-phase evidence covers adaptive quantization-parameter setting for video (ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb); it does not yet cover on-device mixed-precision scheduling or thermal-aware inference prior art, which the finalist-specific audit re-search must retrieve.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- technical_feasibility: Every building block already ships on device - mixed-precision (8/4/2-bit) NPU kernels, activation-range calibration, and thermal/power-state sensors - so the effort is integration and control-loop tuning rather than new hardware; the main feasibility risk is the online sensitivity proxy's stability. Coverage: Feasibility is judged from the mechanism's reliance on already-available NPU capabilities; the research corpus does not directly benchmark such a control loop, a gap the audit does not close since it is prior-art retrieval, not measurement.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- utility_significance: Directly targets the profile's stated problem - KV-cache memory and thermal budgets causing latency spikes for long contexts - by trading precision for energy and latency stability under thermal load, a first-order concern for sustained on-device decoding. Coverage: Utility is grounded in the profile's observed problem and expertise; the evidence corpus confirms the domain's activity but does not quantify the specific energy/latency trade, which remains an empirical open question.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_00c008c63d4f2ceb]
- Described differences from the closest retrieved reference:
  - A per-layer quantization-sensitivity estimator drives an adaptive precision controller that sets each layer's bit-width per decode step, smoothed across decode steps for continuity and biased downward by an NPU thermal-feedback loop. — synthesis operation transfer; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_e532da120d690723]
  - A per-layer bit-width schedule for each decode step and the resulting quantized generated tokens. — synthesis operation transfer; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_e532da120d690723]
  - Full-precision per-layer weights and activations are mapped to a per-layer, per-decode-step variable bit-width representation derived from smoothed sensitivity and thermal signals. — synthesis operation transfer; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_e532da120d690723]
### 2. Large-page-backed, growth-aware KV-cache allocator with precision-tiered cold-entry migration for on-device NPU inference [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- differentiation: The huge-page memory-management reference (ev_019c344b7b377649) optimizes a one-time, install-time allocation of static LLM weights on a server GPU; this candidate's delta is applying large-page backing to the dynamically growing KV-cache with on-demand eviction and a precision-tiered cold pool - a moving, decode-time target the reference does not treat. Coverage: Research-phase evidence covers huge-page allocation for static LLM weights; it does not cover dynamic KV-cache allocators or precision-tiered eviction on NPUs, a gap for the audit re-search to probe.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- technical_feasibility: Large-page allocation and DMA-descriptor control are platform-specific on mobile NPUs, so portability is a real risk; the growth/eviction logic and per-head attention-recency tracking are otherwise straightforward, giving moderate overall feasibility. Coverage: Feasibility depends on NPU memory-system features (large pages, descriptor control) that the research corpus does not enumerate per platform; this hardware-portability question is outside what prior-art retrieval can settle.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- utility_significance: KV-cache memory is the profile's central pain point; keeping per-token latency flat as context grows and extending resident context within a fixed memory budget is highly valuable for long-context on-device use. Coverage: Utility maps directly onto the profile's observed problem; the corpus establishes that KV-cache memory is an active concern but does not measure the allocator's latency-slope benefit.. Coverage limitations: Preliminary pre-audit assessment based only on research-phase retrieval; the finalist-specific live KIPRIS audit has not yet run.. Gaps: none. [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
- Described differences from the closest retrieved reference:
  - A large-page-backed allocator appends KV growth into the active large page and faults a new large page only at milestones, while a tiering manager migrates cold KV entries into a separate quantized large-page pool. — synthesis operation adapt; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
  - A large-page-resident KV-cache layout plus a demoted quantized cold-KV pool with an on-demand restore path. — synthesis operation adapt; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_019c344b7b377649]
  - A per-token growing KV stream is packed into a bounded set of large pages, and cold full-precision KV entries are transformed into lower-precision cold-pool entries. — synthesis operation adapt; described as differing on the differentiation axis [@ev_019c344b7b377649]

## 9 User Decisions at Similarity Checkpoints

Not applicable: no excessive-similarity user checkpoint arose in the current audit.

## 10 Patent-Attorney Handoff Questions and Follow-Up Investigations

### Patent-attorney handoff questions
- For finalist 1, can the NPU thermal and power-state feedback control input be claimed as an independent limitation distinguishing it from per-layer quantization references that carry no runtime thermal signal?
- For finalist 2, does the shift from static, install-time large-page allocation of model weights to dynamic, decode-time KV-cache growth with precision-tiered cold-entry migration support an independent claim over the retrieved memory-management references?
- For finalist 3, is the transfer of context-adaptive quantization-parameter coding from video/audio bitstreams to on-device transformer KV and weight metadata, using transformer-structure contexts, a distinguishable limitation that can be claimed independently?
### Recommended follow-up investigations
- Re-run the finalist-specific KIPRIS audit with additional Korean and English synonyms (for example NPU thermal throttling, mixed-precision scheduling, paged KV cache) to widen coverage beyond the current corpus.
- Search non-KIPRIS sources (arXiv, USPTO, EPO) for on-device mixed-precision and KV-cache-management prior art, since the current corpus is Korean-patent-only.
- Prototype each finalist to empirically quantify the described effects (energy per token, per-token latency slope, bytes per token) before any claim drafting.
